--- 帖子 #1204 ---
Hi Fellow Forex Traders.

Although I am new to this site, I am not new to this system and have traded it successfully for a long time. This system is the best system I have ever traded and it brings me excellent daily results.

My system is the basic system, simple and easy without the pivots and fibs. I have the same set up as renasdad, with one exception. I don't have the luxury of the 4 hour charts to view. Knowing that my setups are easy, I can then concentrate on more currency pairs to watch.

I have www.fxsol.com for a broker which with the new AccuCharts, I can easily watch 20 currency pairs. The only downfall is that I do not have 4 hour charts that I can watch and I make up for it by having a 15 minute, 30 minute and hourly charts. (20 currency pairs X 3 time frames = 60 charts I flip thought with ease using my computer mouse).

When I started out with this system, I watched my favorite currency pair, the EUR/USD. Once I understood what made the pair move, when it moved, the daily average range, etc... and I felt comfortable with it, I started watching a second currency. I worked myself up to 20 currency pairs.

I scan all 20 currency pairs and jump in when all three of my timeframes (15 min, 30 min and hourly charts) are about to converge at the 21 RSI.. 50 line and has successfully crossed it while also looking at the 5/12 crossover and 18/28 convergence tunnels. To prevent confusion, I have an index card with the steps I need to do and the order I need to do them in when I have a possible trade. That way, I don't forget anything.

I must use trailing stops which helps me when I have more than 2 currencies to trade at one time. If I am away from the computer at any time, I will not leave my trading station until trailing stops are set. The forex has a nasty way of moving a hundred pips in the opposite direction during the time it takes you to answer the phone if your not careful. The most currencies I trade at a time can be up to 10. Anymore than that, I am asking for trouble, especially around news time.

Once you have used this sytem with one currency pair and feel that you understand it and can trade it successfully, consider watching a second currency pair and so forth.

I did use pivot points and fibs as a test, but they took way too long to set up and prevented me from watching my charts. I doubt if they could make me anymore pips if I did use them. I went back to the simple basic setup and have not deviated since.

My currency pairs that I watch on a daily basis are:

AUD/CAD AUD/JPY AUD/NZD AUD/USD CAD/JPY CHF/JPY

EUR/AUD EUR/CAD EUR/CHF EUR/GBP EUR/JPY EUR/USD

GBP/CHF GBP/JPY GBP/USD NZD/JPY NZD/USD USD/CAD

USD/CHF AND USD/JPY.

I have a spiral 5" x 8" Ruled Index Cards that has important notes relating to my trading. I suggest that you purchase one too. Get to know the currency pairs, trading times, news times, daily average ranges, which pairs work in conjunction with each other and reverse also.

Ever heard of the term, "Knowledge is Power"? ... In the forex, "Knowledge is Money".

Good luck trading and remember, no question is dumb. At one point, everyone of us did not even know what the word "forex" even meant.

--- 帖子 #1205 ---
Tick,

How do you use the 15 min and 30 min to make your trade on 1 hr charts?

--- 帖子 #1206 ---
In reference to your question "How do you use the 15 min and 30 min to make your trade on 1 hr charts?", what I do is to watch the 15 min, 30 min an hourly chart. Usually, the 15 min chart will have a crossing before the 30 min and hour chart at the RSI 21...50 line. I then check and wait for the 30 min line to cross, followed by the hourly cross at the RSI 21...50 line.

When all three cross, I verify by watching the EMA 5/12 cross each other and look for a crossing or a narrowing of the 18/28 RSI also. When all three move at the same time, I feel comfortable in jumping in, or out of my move.

Anotherwords, the 15 minute movement at the 50 tells me to start watching the 30 minute and then check the hourly chart also. I call my 15 minute and 30 minute charts, my primer charts.

As in drag car racing... here is the way I look at it:

15 minute chart line crosses the RSI 21... 50 line
"Dragster approaches the line to drag race"

30 minute chart line crosses the RSI 21... 50 line
"Dragster then spins his tires getting traction awaiting the green light"

Hourly chart line crosses the RSI 21... 50 line (along with ema 5/12, 18/28 convergences.
"Dragster takes off at green light and races toward the win"

Does this make sense to you?

CT

they rev up the engine for the big movement...which is the entering of the trade. If all three cross, I am in.... not one out of three nor two out of three... all three timeframes must agree.

Chck out a test of all three time frames... and you will see the difference in jumping in when all three time frames agree for entry of a trade.

Please let me know what you think.

Tick

--- 帖子 #1207 ---
I do understand what you are saying.  Wouldn't all three happen though if the 1 hr happens?  Once you get both crosses on the 1 hr, wouldn't we know that the crosses happened on the 15 and 30?    Or do you use the 15 and the 30 to get yourself ready for the 1 hr?

--- 帖子 #1208 ---
Keeping in mind that all three charts would not be in unison in reference to time, the 15 minute would show the possibility of a movement before the 30 minute and hourly chart. The 15 usually crosses before the other two time frames.

There are at times when they will not totally agree and maybe off by 30 minutes.... but I do watch the 15 minutes which prepares me for the 30 minute to move only on the hourly chart.

The reason why I don't move on the 15 minute chart which usually crosses the RSI 21... 50 mid line first is because the 15 minute is like an ocean wave, it can cross the RSI 21... 50 line and you would assume that it is profit time and wham, it will return under the RSI 21... 50 line and you lost pips.

Hope this give you a better understanding.

Tick

--- 帖子 #1226 ---
What everybody here fails to realize is that you are looking at the chart unrealisticaly. The EMAs and the WMAs are all closing values. MEANING that you would open your position at the end of each period (closing price). Everybody is counting the opening price, but this is wrong, because the indicators will not be what they are at open. The only cross this system is somewhat successful at is GBP/JPY... test it, run it on a demo account, and you'll see what I am talking about

--- 帖子 #1252 ---
I am new to Forex / MQ4, still in learning phase...

I made 2 files, 1 for WMA(1hr) and 1 for EMA (30Mins).

WMA/EMA/SMA/RiskLevel are changeable in the input area

MA1/MA2 = Sidus Tunel (Red)

MA3/MA4 = Trade Indictor (Green/Blue)

Risk Level = please refer to Vegas 1hr Docs, only 2 lines is available due to 8 lines limit....(Or you can apply this indicator twice for another 2 lines)

PS:You don't need to close and re-open to activate the new indicator.

Copy the mq4 file into indicator folder, open it with metaeditor and click on compile.  It should now shows in your indicator folder inside MT4 (if not, double click the indicator folder in MT4 twice).

OK now i'm up to post 325...hehe. Just my 2 pips worth on bonmeister's great post. I've been using what i call "4d" charts (time is known as the fourth demension) for a while now. --- 帖子 #1276 ---
The differant risk models will puut fib lines  (X) amount of pips from the tunnel.  The more volatile a pair is, the higher the risk model.  The best thing to do is put a tunnel on your chart and zoom out as far as you can.   The right risk model will be where the price reaches the outter fibs and then retraces back towards the tunnel.

--- 帖子 #1279 ---
EMA = exponential moving average

WMA = weighted moving average (or linear weighted moving average on MT4) meaning it gives more weighting to more recent numbers

On MT4 click on Indicators, Moving average, and then you will see the diffrent types of moving average you can select.

--- 帖子 #1282 ---
Bagovino, here is the short extract from Vegas:

I have scripted a plug-in called ‘Vegas Currency Daily’ to use on the daily charts. It will plot and draw the tunnel EMA’s as well as various fib levels [three on each side of the tunnel per model #]. When you open ‘Vegas Currency Daily’ you have 4 input models [fib numbers] to choose from. They are as follows:

<?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /><o></o>

Model #1 = 89, 144, 233

Model #2 = 144, 233, 377

Model #3 = 233, 377, 610

Model #4 = 377, 610, 987

[Note: I have included the plug-in with your email, so you can create the appropriate metatrader 4 charts immediately.]

<o></o>

For the following currency pairs, use the following model # on your daily chart.

<o></o>

EUR/USD - Model # 1 AND Model #2. Overlay #2 after you have setup Model #1. Just go back and do #2. This will now produce an overlap of #1 and #2

And produce 4 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 8]. You will now have fib numbers calculated at 89, 144, 233, and 377 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

GBP/USD - Model #1 AND Model #3. Overlay #3 after you have setup Model #1.

You now have 5 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 10].

The fib numbers are calculated at 89, 144, 233, 377, and 610 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

USD/CHF - Model #2. You now have 3 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 6]. The fib numbers are calculated at 144, 233, and 377 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

USD/JPY - Model # 1. You now have 3 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 6]. The fib numbers are calculated at 89, 144, and 233 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

AUD/USD - Model # 1. You now have 3 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 6]. The fib numbers are calculated at 89, 144, and 233 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

USD/CAD - Model #2. You now have 3 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 6]. The fib numbers are calculated at 144, 233, and 377 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

EUR/JPY - Model #2. You now have 3 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 6]. The fib numbers are calculated at 144, 233, and 377 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

EUR/GBP - Model # 1. You now have 3 fib lines on both sides of the tunnel [for a total of 6]. The fib numbers are calculated at 89, 144, and 233 from the daily tunnel.

<o></o>

Step 3.

<o></o>

We are interested only when the market gets to the following fib numbers per appropriate currency pair. They are as follows:

<o></o>

EUR/USD - When it reaches the third fib level [233] or higher.

GBP/USD - The third fib level [233] and higher.

USD/CHF - The second fib level [233] and higher.

USD/JPY - The second fib level [144] and higher.

AUD/USD - The second fib level [144] and higher.

USD/CAD - The second fib level [233] and higher.

EUR/JPY - The second fib level [233] and higher.

EUR/GBP - The first fib level [89] and higher.

<o></o>

Once these fib levels are breached, we now look for specific technical indicators that signal a reverse in trend. These are [in no importance of order] 1) Reversals, 2) Spinning Tops, 3) Hammer and/or Hanging man, and 4) Inverted Hammer and/or Shooting Star

For more detail information about Vegas, it is best to read the whole from Vegas wealth builder section.

Renasdad and Artamon have mentioned that they take signals either close to the 1h tunnel or countertrend signals near the 1h outer fib levels. Having only glanced at the EurGbp just now, you're correct. Its daily AverageTrueRange(10) is frequently below 30. I suppose the tunnel (144 and 169 ema's) could also be altered to suit the currency pair so that the "model" fits better. Just my initial thoughts.

--- 帖子 #1317 ---
Hey Bagovino take it easy we were just jocking a little, it's all good

Well, since you say I provide no contributions on this thread, here it comes:

Whatever method you use (original Sidus or Bagovino's) make sure that before placing your trade, on all (if not most) time frames your trade points in the same direction.

If you use a 1 hr chart, then look at the long time frame like 8hr to see where the major trend is going, BUT also make sure to look at 30min or even 15 min to see if the are any major changes in the orizon for the next couple of hours...

This is a hard thing to back test 'cause it would be a mess to keep up with different times frames at the same time while scrolling down charts, but I can talk for personal experience and it works wonders, and it gives you more confidence in placing the trade.

Many times the Sidus method and the Bagovino's method give signals that are not confirmed by the other time frames. In those situations the methods seem to fail the most.

So the right procedure should be to use a 1hr chart and look for either a Sidus or Bagovino signal, once you find it THEN you look at all the other time frames for confirmation....

Just my two cents

Future

Without exception, it is the people who are too lazy to read a thread from start to finish,who seek to destroy the concept of trial & error.

These people are lookng for the "Holy Grail".

I have good news for these people. The "Holy Grail" exists, but most of them will have given up trading long before they have the chance to discover the secret of it.

1. Trading without incurring losses doesn't exist !

2. Endless searching for the perfect entry system is a waste of time.

3. Cluttering your screen with multiple indicators will only confuse.

4. Try this in DEMO toss a coin, use heads for long  entry, tails for short  entry. Use a 10pip stop & a 20pip take profit. Let trade run until stop or limit is hit, then enter again on a new toss of the coin. This idea is used as a MM example by Woodie.

BabeFX.

--- 帖子 #1334 ---
SinarFX, firstly Sidus system originally posted here, is based on similar concept of Vegas 1hr tunnel, but is no where close the the tunnel ema's of Vegas 1hr tunnel, and secondly "RSI= Vegas 1hr Tunnel"  is not a valid statement that you made. Dont compare an indicator with a System.

RSI is used to filter out weak or false ema crosses in general, not in particular to Vegas or Sidus.

5ema and 12ema is introduced by Bogovino and he uses RSI(21) to filter false crosses. so RSI is most important in this 5/12 cross.

--- 帖子 #1390 ---
First post.    I want to thank Sidus for this kick ass method -- I seriously believe this baby is going to help me achieve financial independence.

Anyway, I will write a little bit about my experiences with the original Sidus method as well as attach an mt4 I made.

I've been lurking this thread for awhile and have read every single post up to about page 75 of this thread.  I used Bago's method at first, because of the "newer is better" mentality.  Unfortunately, I got chopped up pretty badly (I always trade live btw), and have since reverted to the original Sidus.  What I found out is that it gives the many of the same good signals of my old method of trading (CCI 50 + EMA 34 aka 5034 method from tradershaven.net), but it has far less bad trades.  I did my own experimenting and found that crosses on the zero line of the CCI50 corresponded to crosses of the RSI21, so I programmed both into my MT4 file to as a filter for the Sidus signals.  I have been using this for entries with excellent results on 1 hr. chart on usd pairs, and am experimenting using 4 hr. charts on jpy pairs.  For exits, I exit based on absolute fibonacci (http://www.leftbraintrading.com/).  Absolute fibonacci is pretty cool, because... you just don't know why it works, but it does.  o_O  Same reason why fibonacci works in nature for no apparent reason?  *shrug*  Left brain trading has an mt4 file, but since he's making his livelihood selling his $30 book + mt4 file (a steal imho), I don't feel at liberty to post it here.

Anyway, here is the mt4 that I made for the Sidus method.  Credits are given in at the beginning of the file to Sidus as well as the person I used the mt4 file as a template.  It detects when the wma's cross the tunnel (arrows) as well as when the tunnel crosses (dots) and is filtered by both RSI and CCI.  If you want to remove the filters, just delete the lines that look like this:

RSI > 50 &&

CCI > 0 &&

and recompile or save it and reload metatrader.  You can set it so that it gives sound alerts and/or e-mail alerts.  Note that you have to turn on sound alerts ("Alerts" input) to get e-mail alerts (sorry, too busy trading it to program it further).

I hope this mt4 file can help someone out like how it has helped me -- and Sidus, thank you thank you thank you, and thank you for coming back to this thread!  Hopefully I can quit being a lab rat soon (scientific researchers get paid less than toilet scrubbers btw).  Looking forward to Sidus v2!

Take care and many prayers to all of you, my trading friends.

Anthony

--- 帖子 #1391 ---
Hi,

this is my first post at forexfactory... I was reading your posts last couple of days, got to page 16 and then skipped to the last.

Sidus (12 EMA instead of 8 EMA + 21 RSI) system is nice and simple.

I did get some ideas about entry and exit points, I didnt do a lot of testing because I was very busy but I think they could be helpfull:

1. entry point - besides MA crossing, I think it is good to use additional horizontal RSI lines, 45  and 55. So, for long, enter is 5 and 12 EMAs cross AND RSI cross 55 line from below.For short is vice versa... I also noticed that it is good to use two charts, for example, 1H chart for general enter point and 15M for precise enter point.

2. exit point - Problem with MA crossing system (Parabolic SAR also) is that you can get to the same point where you started the position although  there was a nice profit  between two crosses which was not taken. One solution is trailing stop, another is to set target and wait ( also good to take some profit on the run, like 50% at 10 pips, another 25% at 20 and so on..) and the third one is (if I remember correctly, please check it) to wait when RSI crosses 50 line (or 55 and 45  , i really do not remember).

Comments are welcome...

Ferovca

--- 帖子 #1394 ---
Short Answer:

Better results with 12ema.

Detailed Answer:

As mentioned I tested "Sidus" with 1 lot, live, shorting one of the more "exotic" pairs, AUD/NZD with its 12 pip spread and my having absolutely no knowledge as to how the pair behaves or what time of day is best for trading it. "Sidus" worked fine, particularly when you monitor emas crossing first on the 15M, then 30M, and finally on 1H charts (Tick's contribution). RSI(21) with the 50 crossing before the emas cross, is an additional confirmation but one can trade successfully without it but watch out for "whipsaws".

Further confirmation of "Sidus". Friday morning, 8 Sept 2006 following the Canadian news regarding employment, I was long 1 lot USD/JPY with a 30 pip SL, based on emas (5,12,18,28) crossing first in the 15m, then the 30m, then the 1H. In other words, 5ema had entered the tunnel or river created by the 18 and 28 on all three charts. Beautiful textbook signal.

But then the pair reversed and after probably 20 minutes between 10-15 pips in the red, I decided to close and reverse, going short. Of course after another 20-25 minutes, the pair reversed again and went long, only to plateau at my original entry. So down 20 or so pips (due to the close-and-reverse), I decided to liquidate the position. Probably 30 minutes later I noticed the pair fulfilled my original long TP and more!!! In other words, once again "Sidus" worked, I just didn't patiently wait it out. (NewsTrader at heart: fast, furious and phenomenally profitable!! Adapting to these 3 hour, 3 day, 3 month moves, which while not fast and furious, can also be phenoms!!!)

Conclusion

Good system, capable of consistently profitable results.

Just information; not a recommendation. Individual results may vary depending on experience, skill level, aversion to risk, capitalization and cognitive capabilities.  Forex trading is inherently risky and not suitable for some children nor for many, many adults!

This is just a suggestion.

I'm glad some people liked the indicator.  ^^  Attached to this message are some buzzer wavs that I use to wake myself (and the neighbors) up in case of a signal.  You should only use this if you are confident you could shake off a sleepy head within 2-3 minutes, effectively analyze the markets, place your trade, then go back to sleep.

Anyway, I forgot to say some things in my last post.  This is long (I like to write.... a lot....), so I'll divide it into sections.

How the MT4 Indicator Works

I suggest adding the actual ema 18/28 to see how fat the tunnel is and entering on the signal only if the tunnel is thin or about to cross. I tried programming to make it draw the EMAs, but for some reason, I can't get it to work...

Also, if you scroll back too far, the arrows and dots get all whacky and get placed all over... I don't know how to fix that.  Just close and reopen metatrader or recompile the indicator using MetaEditor.

So how the indicator works...  The dots are pretty simple -- they just tell you when the ema18/28 crosses with no filter.  Sometimes entering based solely on a tunnel cross works, sometimes it doesn't (NZD/JPY seem to work well on Tunnel crosses, but please use your own discretion).  If you are entering in based solely on tunnel crosses all the time, then please re-read the Sidus system.

For the arrows, it happens when the WMAs cross both tunnel lines.  This is the actual signal to get in -- please correct me if I'm wrong.  The arrow is displayed on the close of the candle, thus you would get in on the next candle after the arrow.  Many times I see the candle after the arrow retrace a little, allowing you a better entry point to breakeven with the spread.  These arrows are filtered with RSI + CCI, which you can remove if you like.

How I Close & What I Do in Loss

I actually use both the Sidus tunnel and absolute fibs to close.  If I get in on a signal and am in loss, I do one of two things:

1.  If soon after my entry, the Sidus tunnel crosses (dot) or I get a full signal (arrow) both the other way (crap), I know I'm in for more losses, so I close or close & reverse.

2.  If I don't see or hear a cross/signal, I just stick out any losses I have incurred.  You have to give something to gain something, you know?

As for the absolute fibs, I know I should stay in until the next Sidus tunnel cross (the original method), but keeping in mind the lagging aspect, price action would have to retrace quite a lot OR it would have to channel for some time and then retrace before the tunnels will cross.  Either way would cut into profits.  Thus, I decided to use absolute fibs instead.  At every fib line, I exit out a portion of my trade, move up my stoplosses and let the rest run to lock in profits.

If you don't have or don't want to pay $30 to learn about absolute fibs, then I guess partial take profits at 10-30 pip increments (depending on the pair) would do the same thing.  Please don't kick yourself and think, "I should've stayed in longer!" (I say that, but I do it all the time)    Over the long run, you're locking in profits better -- that's what I think.

Some Notes

As with any indicator, you will get false signals.  Use whatever experience you have to decide whether or not to enter the trade.  I never (or at least try not to) enter in blindly or use indicators as set rules.  In essence, there are no set rules for a fluid market that's ever changing and adapting.  Like Money Ma$ter (and yes, I read about the CC e-mail guy; sad...), I was a news trader in the past before the evilbrokers caught on and started putting me in loss, so I do use some fundamental basis to see which direction I should be trading.  On pairs I am not familiar with, I use some technicals (i.e. daily highs lows, monthly highs lows, which fib price likes to hang around, etc) to see which direction I should be trading.  Really, imho, it is best to not rely completely on an indicator, but to use your brain and all the experiences you've learned to place a confident trade.  I think that's the best filter you can get out there.  ^^

Whew - Best Wishes ><

Anyway, thanks, Money Ma$ter, for wishing me blessings.  Man, do I need em! ^^  I know there are other people like me who are doing this not only for themselves, but their families and loved ones.  Regardless of whether you're doing this as a hobby or to provide, I will continue to pray for all of you.  There is a way for us to win, and we can conquer this beast called forex -- just trust and believe in God, and trust and believe in yourself.  Not many people can read through thousands and thousands of posts, put in endless hours watching charts, watching Bloomberg, following economic indicators, and pouring in sweat and blood for this.   We deserve to be wealthy and happy, and we are all blessed to live in a place that gives us that chance.  Don't ever forget to appreciate yourself and the effort you placed -- even during loss.

Ok, so that's my (long) rant.  lol  Take care everyone!

--- 帖子 #1412 ---
For all those using the EMACrossover indicator as well as the Sidus indicators I posted, and perhaps others that signal moving average crosses, the following procedure will allow you to scroll back and forth without whacking out the offending indicator and having it place signals all over your chart.

The reason seems to be Metatrader's multitasking limitations -- it's trying to download data while at the same time applying the rules of the indicator, making it confused and out of its mind.

So how to get around this that we may backtest any such MT4 indicator?

Short Version Remove the indicator CTRL-O -> Charts tab -> Change "Max bars in history" and "Max bars in chart" to 250000 Turn off Autoscroll Scroll all the way back on chart allowing Metatrader to download data. Re-add indicator Long Version (The Dummy's Guide lol)Remove the offending indicator: Hit CTRL-I, click on the indicator, and click Delete.  Now click Close. Hit CTRL-O (that's O like in "Open") and go to the Charts tab Change "Max bars in history" to 250000. Change "Max bars in chart" to 250000. Hit OK Go to the Charts menu and turn off Autoscroll. On the chart, scroll ALL the way back, as far as the chart will go.  This will make Metatrader download all the chart data.  You will see how much data is being downloaded in your connection status. Scroll back and forth on the chart -- it should be smooth and quick, since Metatrader is no longer downloading data. You may now re-add the indicator:  Insert (menu) -> Indicators -> Custom -> Name_of_My_Offending_Indicator. Voila!  Now you can scroll back and forth for 2 years (on hourly chart) without your indicators going all whacky! Note that you will need to repeat this procedure if you change timeframes and/or chart pairs.

I am now backtesting the Sidus method (or well, the mt4 indicator I posted that's based on the original Sidus).  My conclusion so far (Jan-Mar 2004)?  It's good - even after denting it with worst case scenarios and inefficiencies.  It's so good, it's almost too good to be true...  It worked two years ago and it's working now...  I just... I feel like... like I'm gonna cry, man.  ;__;  ...finally... A tech method that works and keeps brokers from messing with me.  I can survive without fundamentals...  I'm so... so happy...   You da man, Sidus.  **sniff**  You da maaaan!!!  **cry**

Hot dang.

Anyway, after I finish backtesting, I'll post my spreadsheet.  =D  And yes yes, I know that past performance is no guarantee of future results; blah blah blah.  But it worked, had worked, and is working, so get it while it's hot, right?  ^^

Yes, I'm finally shutting up for now lol  ><

L8rz,

--- 帖子 #1422 ---
If you are confused, I would say to stick with the WMA's as WMA's are more evenly weighted than EMA's resulting in more "accurate" moving averages. Thusly, you should get more quality signals.

Bago's EMA method is a way for him to jump the gun by a few degrees, so to speak. He tends to be right more often than not, but the WMA will give you that little bit more safety since it is a bit more conservatively computed.

--- 帖子 #1423 ---
Hollis is essentially correct.

Original Sidus used 5,8 WMAs and 18/28 EMAs, preferably on the 1H but could be used on 30M chart (see first post, attached PDF).  Over time, this evolved into 5,12,18,28 EMAs with RSI(21) as confirmation when greater (long) or less (short) than 50.  Renasdad summarized the evolved Sidus in his journal (see below):

The Following is from renasdad at ForexFactory.com<?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /><o></o>
<TT>Here is a run down of the sidus system.  I like to call it "3Phase".  It has three phases to it. </TT>

<TT>When talking about this, I will talk all in buying.  For selling, just switch it around. </TT>

<TT>Phase 1 </TT>

<TT>On a 30 minute chart, you need a 5 EMA and 12 EMA.  Also,  RSI(21 period)  with a level 50 line. </TT>
<TT>Those are the only indicators needed on a 30 minute chart. </TT>

<TT>What to look for on phase 1 </TT>

<TT>5 EMA will cross 12 EMA from below to above.  RSI needs to go above 50.  Wait for a candle close before taking a trade.  This guarantees it wasn't a fake signal. </TT>
<TT>so, for phase 1  5 crosses the 12 going up.  RSI crosses 50 going up. </TT>

<TT>Phase 2 </TT>

<TT>Once a trade is opened, switch to the 1 hr charts. </TT>

<TT>This is what you need on a 1 hr chart. </TT>
<TT>5/12/18/28   All EMAs    I am looking into the RSI for use on the 1 hr chart but for now, I only use these EMAs </TT>

<TT>What to look for on phase 2 </TT>

<TT>5 EMA crosses 12 EMA Which will then cross the 18/28 EMA.  If the 5 and 12 EMA cross the 18/28 EMAs that is confirmation of trend. </TT>

<TT>Phase 3 </TT>

<TT>This phase is for taking profits.  This differs with people.  It depends on how they like to trade.  For me, I like Vegas 1 hr tunnel.  Some use support/resistance,  some use Fib levels. </TT>

There was additional evolution after this point but as I read the thread the additional tweaks only confused many.  Using either Original Sidus or Evolved Sidus will work.  Hope that clears things up.

--- 帖子 #1439 ---
I don't know if anyone here has read the Mechanical Discretion methods but one thing used for a MA cross system is a breakout of two consecutive candles of the same color with the second candle passing the first.  In other words once the 5 crosses up the 12 you would look for the first blue (in my case) candle - which may be the candle on the cross.  Then you would look for the next candle to surpass that candles high before entering a trade.  He goes further to state that the "breakout" candle needs to happen within the next two candles, but I was never really that strict.

I think if you back test this you'll see numerous occassions where this has prevented entry into a trade that would not have made it.  It also prevents the need for later crossing of other MA's IMHO.

Just thought I'd add some more thought to the process.. :-)

Jason

I'd recommend also looking at the PDF from the very first post.

Sidus says:

I don't want to jump the gun, but I think it went a bit like this...

Sidus used to use 5 and 8 WMA and now version 2 will use 5 and 12 WMA instead. No idea whether on close or median or what, but I assume on close.  And he didn't enter when the 5 crossed the 8 or now the 12, but when that happened and THEN both crossed the 18/28 combo, when the 18/28 pair was squeezed together tight, as this makes the best trades.

(basically this just represents that the market has stopped whatever it was doing and is now trying to decide on a new direction and the crossing of the fast WMAs past the slower EMAs tries to interpret this as a decision to "go somewhere" and tries to ride the momentum. this is the reason for me advocating small stops...)

As opposed to bagovino, Sidus waits for the WMAs to actually move past the 18/28 pair first, whereas correct RSI (<>50) and the fast EMA cross of 5 and 12 alone is enough for bagovino . Correct me if I am wrong here.

More safety I think is his(Sidus') reason. It does make you miss pips occasionally, but I assume he saw it also prevent fake signals?  Haven't spent that much time looking into it...

Also Sidus uses 5 and 12 WMA, bago believes in EMA...to each his own, to be honest there isn't exactly that much difference, both give fake signals and need some amount of discretion and/or experience or just plain good old money management to allow for these fakes without thinking twice...

IMHO using good MM you can take any and all signals and still end up winning as long as you make at least 1:1 and > 50% of all signals work...adjust r/r and % accordingly and statistics are your friend

The RSI 50 thing is just an attempt to get more reassurance that things are bullish or bearish when the crossings happen..

Oh and one last thing, the reason some trades lately that weren't actually proper signals if you consider RSI worked out was because nippy or EJ for example showed a pin bar and these two systems both get you into a pin bar trade early or at the same time as the pin breaks....funny coincidence ;D But it works

A case where price action and MA cross systems coincide

I hope the confusion is now complete ;D

--- 帖子 #1465 ---
After studying the charts, it is apparant that the bagovino system, and sidus's system are essentially identical.

Both use a 5/12 cross. (Granted they differ on the use of EMA vs LWMA)

Sidus uses 18/28 EMAs to determine the long term trend.

Bagovino uses a 21 period RSI.

Place sidus's 18/28 EMA's on any chart, and then place a 21 RSI on the same chart.

Notice anything?

I'll tell you...

LONG:

As soon as the 5/12 cross, and price touches the 18/28 EMA's going up, and they cross, (Sidus's real GO signal), RSI goes positive. And as long as the 18/28 tunnel is BELOW the price, RSI will remain positive.

SHORT:

As soon as As soon as the 5/12 cross, and price touches the 18/28 EMA's going down, and they cross, (Sidus's real GO signal), RSI goes negative. And as long as the 18/28 tunnel is ABOVE the price, RSI will remain negative.

Depends on the flavour you like, but ice cream is ice cream.

Thank you Sidus.

Hello SeekingLight,

Sorry I haven't tried using 15 pip SL on 4H yet.  I trade 1H according to the mighty Sidus sytem.  I still use the RSI 21 though before I enter but once I'm in I  remove all other indicators and just watch the candles jump up and down.  :

As for setting SL and TP on opening, I use a figure rounded to 10 because it allows me to execute rapidly.   For example the price is at 1.2650 and I want to go long I simply delete the 2nd to the last digit (5 in this case) and substitute 2 to make 1.2620 to give me 30 pips SL.  I do the same with TP by adding 40,  quickly changing 5 to 9 to give me 1.2690.  No complicated calculations  allowing me to execute in a few seconds and depending on movement can save me a few pips.  I just keep in mind the two numbers + or -30 and + or -40 and make necessary adjustments once I'm the trade.

Sidus, thanks for sharing this system.  You'll never know how much you changed peoples lives and their familes and friends and grandsons and granddaughters.  Infinite blessings be upon you!

To all the wonderful people who never tire of sharing you will harvest great abundance!

--- 帖子 #1510 ---
On the main screen of MT, go to the top tag option and choose Insert->indicators->Trend->Moving Average, then a popup window of moving average is appeared. From there change the option Period to 18, MA method to Exponential. Use the same method apply to each chart window ( that is each currency pair windows ).

Once is done. Do the same for selecting the 28 EMA.

--- 帖子 #1514 ---
The indicator uses EMAs. What follows is an excerpt of that code:

// Original Sidus Method filtered with RSI and CCI.
// Edited by Anthony Pham using EMA-Crossover_Signal.mq4 as a

// template.
//(Jason Robinson, jnrtrading, http://www.jnrtrading.co.uk)
/*

+------------------------------------------------------------------+

| Shows an arrow when there is a Sidus signal. Shows dots when |

| the Sidus tunnel crosses. Blue dot confirms uptrend. Red dot |

| confirms downtrend. Alerts on Sidus signal by default - Sounds |

| alert and sends e-mail. |

+------------------------------------------------------------------+

*/
extern bool Alerts = true;

extern bool Tunnel_Alerts= false;

extern bool Email_Alerts = false;
#property indicator_chart_window

#property indicator_buffers 4

#property indicator_color1 Aqua

#property indicator_color2 Red

#property indicator_color3 Blue

#property indicator_color4 Red
#property indicator_width1 1

#property indicator_width2 1

#property indicator_width3 1

#property indicator_width4 1
double CrossUp[];

double CrossDown[];

double Tup[];

double Tdown[];

bool DownTunnel = false;

bool UpTunnel = false;

bool Signal = false;
extern int FasterEMA = 5;

extern int SlowerEMA = 12;

extern int FasterSidusEMA = 18;

extern int SlowerSidusEMA = 28;

The SIDUS method incorporates the use of the 5 and 12 WMA, not EMA.  Read back and you will find that SIDUS uses WMA to judge price movement sooner.  The original method was with the 5 and 8 WMA.  Of course you use the 12 and 28 EMA for the tunnel.

Some others have talked about 5 and 12 EMA, but SIDUS reemphasizes the use of 5 and 12 WMA.

The method works for other pairs, but stay with the 1 hour time frame.

Hi all,

Wow it took me a a few days to finish reading this. After much tinkering this is what i can summarise about SIDUS.

1. Good for trend trading.

2. A lot of fake breakouts even after rsi filtering.

3. Subjected to whipsaws.

4. A potential pip harvesting system similar to OCC created by twoblink.

5. Kills you in trendless markets.

All said, i wanted to make a system that could work well during trendless markets and trending market. But how?

Something came to mind after i read Akuma's posts of his Bollinger Breakout system. The system itself averages about 30-100 pips per trade, it potentially rides short term trends effectively but misses out on the long term trend. A good scalping system

And this is my solution to it. Combine both techniques to maximise both trending and trendless ,market.

Akuma uses a rainbow mma which is a great tool. You could recognize the change in trends just by looking at how the mma slopes form. This will be THE MOST IMPORTANT tool in this new system. He also used the bollinger squeeze indicator to check short term accumulation, which i will incorporate into the new system. I will also instead use an RSI 9 instead of the proposed 21 to maximise oscillation plays.

Am i right to say that this is how market works .....consolidate-trend-consolidate-trend etc etc....

so this is my preposition.....

Hi Jest,

1. Start your own thread, because the system-mix seems to deserve that much, and work on it to see how it goes

2. Be aware that you might be falling into the traps that a lot of beginners fall into: wanting to ALWAYS trade and make profit and wanting a system that has a truckload of indicators to have more reassurance. The market seems complicated, so you need a complicated system, right? (I'd say: not really)

But of course you can complicate things and still end up winning, which is why I suggested starting something yourself, you seem to have a good eye for ideas and new ideas are always worth considering and developing in any matter.

I respect the effort put into it and if you think it's a good thing then go for it!

Best wishes & good luck,

--- 帖子 #1536 ---
I've only checked back briefly on a few pairs (Euro,Pound and Swissy vs. USD) but I've noticed that when the indicator EA  AX512EMACROSSw/RSI (posted somewhere earlier) has an Arrow (the cross) and a Dot (the RSI) both on the SAME bar the percentage of good trades is increased. The following bars most always go in favorable direction. This means fewer trades to be taken but with a higher percent of winners you can trade less often with more size. Maybe someone here will be interested in checking this out with more focus as I've only gave it a brief passing investigation. Also it could be exanded to include trading when the two events are within one bar of each other instead of only on the same one hour bar. I would think this is the result of higher volitility hence bigger moves that result. Also from what I could see this tends not to happen during a consolidation which could help protect from whipsaws. IMHO

--- 帖子 #1568 ---
SMA = Simple Moving Average

EMA = Exponential Moving Average

WMA= Weighted Moving Average (or Linear Weighted Moving Average)

Don't ask me to explain them.

Just mess around with them on the chart, and see the differences between them.

OK?

--- 帖子 #1575 ---
Hi Eyevoltage,<?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /><o></o>

<o> </o>

The AMA is called an Adaptive Moving Average, I came across it in some magazine and it looks pretty good. See the attached PDF file for further info.<o></o>

Unfortunately my maths isn’t great and my programming is as bad so can’t explain it to you, but the formulas are all in the PDF file.<o></o>

I’m relatively new to the Forex market (6 months) but learned so much in that time, thanx to forums like this excellent one. I started out using spread betting and haven’t had any problems with it, there are lots of SB brokers out there so it’s a matter of personal preference, but I use the following:<o></o>

<o> </o>

CMC Markets – VERY competitive spreads, 2-3 pips on the majors – Huge selection of currencies etc – Not web based unfortunately, you install their platform onto your PC and it’s not the most user friendly, but OK when you get the hang of it – I use them for any trades that have to be rolled over as they do it automatically and cheaply too.<o></o>

<o> </o>

Finspreads – Almost as competitive with their spreads as CMC – A more limited selection of currencies etc – Web based and good simple interface – I use them for intraday trades only as they are kind of expensive for rolling over trades into the next business day.<o></o>

<o> </o>

Capital Spreads – Very similar to Finspreads, except that they double their spread overnight!!! Don’t use them now because of this but otherwise very good.<o></o>

I’m based in the <?xml:namespace prefix = st1 ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:smarttags" /><st1:country-region><st1lace>UK</st1lace></st1:country-region> and the tax free thing is a big bonus with SB as its regarded as betting, you don’t need as much money either, so it’s easy to start off with a lower bank and you only really use the money itself if you lose a trade. I prefer trading with a real account (you can trade with as little as 50p per pip) as it’s the emotions which are the difficult thing to control, you don’t have this with the demo accounts so it’s a very different experience!

I use MT4 to set up my trades as none of the brokers have decent charts and then just place my trade with my chosen broker. The only thing you don't have with SB is trailing stops, which is a pain.
<o> </o>

Hope this is of some help.<o></o>

<o> </o>

<o> </o>

Regards<o></o>

<o> </o>

DS

--- 帖子 #1579 ---
@ Eyevoltage

As regards the AMA I think I’ve found one in the Metaquotes site, never looked there properly before, follow this link http://codebase.mql4.com/indicators?p=8 and its on P9.

Yup, it’s a great site this, one of my main research points before I started trading, this and the Andy X – Insider Signal course.

I don’t know why more people don’t spread bet, I see nothing but advantages using it.
Maybe it’s the stigma associated with betting!

I only use CMC if I’m either sitting at my home PC OR putting on a trade that will last for more than one day. As I work full-time I can’t monitor the trade 9-5, that’s why I like a web based platform one like Finspreads or Capital, I can keep an eye on things from work.

There is a small difference in prices between MT4 and the SB platforms, varies by broker, but around 2-3 pips, but you can’t get away from that anyway and I haven’t found it to be a problem.

There usually isn’t a big rush to get the trades on unless I’m trading the news releases, in which case I have MT4 open and the SB platform open at the same time. If I’m at work when the news is released I use the basic charts from Finspreads, I get everything set up ready to trade a few minutes before the news release, and when I see the candlestick chart start to move at the appointed time I quickly switch screens and hit the buy or sell button, works pretty well, but you have to move fast before the market reverses as it sometimes does. I’ve found that mechanically straddling the market is pointless in these cases as your order gets filled too late and you end up losing pips. The Non-farm payroll report on the last Friday of the month is a nice easy 100 odd pips for about 15-30 mins work.

With regard to your PC, shouldn’t be a problem having MT4 and your SB platform open at the same time, main thing is that it doesn’t crash when having both open, a fast Broadband connection is probably more important.

My PC spec is a P4 3GHz, 1GB RAM, 260GB HDD running Win XP with a crappy 512KB BB connection (too far from the exchange etc) and I have no problems.

Don’t know about older PC’s, but I don’t think these applications are particularly CPU intensive, best to try it and see how you get on.

Regards
DS

Hi Eyevoltage,

I had a look at e-trade, their spreads seem a bit large, EUR/USD and GBP/USD 6 pips, personally I would be looking for 2-3 pips spread for those two pairs.

To be honest their order fill time of 3-6 seconds is the same as Capital, Finspreads and CMC.

You got it right with the trailing stop, none of the brokers for SB I've seen appear to cater for it which is a real bummer. It does make it more inconvenient as you have to keep changing your stop manually, but no choice there!!

I haven't a clue how the 'proper' trading works involving the lots, mini, standard accounts etc. As far as I can see with SB you don't actually buy or sell anything, unlike the other form of trading, all you are doing is betting on which way the market is going to go, basically the same principle there. For example, if you had £1000 in your SB account, the money is never actually used unless you lose your trade, an amount is usually reserved as margin (deposit) and if you win your trade this margin is made available to you again as well as what you have won. If you had lost your trade the margin is still returned and the amount you had lost would be deducted from your account. It's kinda difficult to explain, sorry.

I think starting our own SB thread would be a great idea, just not sure whereabouts it would go in the forum!! Don't want to hijack this thread!!

Would be nice to get further input from any other spread betters here, if any!

I still haven't had a chance to test the AMA in MT4 but hopefully soon, like you I've been preoccupied with other matters  :-(

Below code is buggy. Anyone here can solve the Sidus-EMA.mq4 attached by GreatYves.

if (

( // Conditions for up signal for EMA-Sidus crosses

(( FasterEMAnow > fasterSidusEMAnow && FasterEMAnow > slowerSidusEMAnow ) ||

( SlowerEMAnow > fasterSidusEMAnow && SlowerEMAnow > slowerSidusEMAnow )) &&

( FasterEMAprevious <= fasterSidusEMAprevious || FasterEMAprevious <= slowerSidusEMAprevious ) &&

( SlowerEMAprevious <= fasterSidusEMAprevious || SlowerEMAprevious <= slowerSidusEMAprevious ) &&

// RSI > 50 &&

// CCI > 0 &&

UpTunnel

)

)

{   // IF all that above is correct, then do this:

UpTunnel=false;

DownTunnel=false;

Signal=true;

CrossUp[i] = Low[i] - Range*1.6;

if(i<=2 && Alerts && !upalert)

{

Alert (Symbol()," ",Period()," Mins  Sidus LONG ");

if ( Email_Alerts ) { SendMail("Sidus LONG "+Symbol(),""); }

upalert=true;

downalert=false;

}

}

if (

( // Conditions for down signal for EMA-Sidus crosses too

(( FasterEMAnow < fasterSidusEMAnow && FasterEMAnow < slowerSidusEMAnow ) ||

( SlowerEMAnow < fasterSidusEMAnow && SlowerEMAnow < slowerSidusEMAnow )) &&

( FasterEMAprevious >= fasterSidusEMAprevious || FasterEMAprevious >= slowerSidusEMAprevious ) &&

( SlowerEMAprevious >= fasterSidusEMAprevious || SlowerEMAprevious >= slowerSidusEMAprevious ) &&

// RSI < 50 &&

// CCI < 0 &&

DownTunnel

)

)

{   // IF all that above is correct, then do this:

UpTunnel=false;

DownTunnel=false;

Signal=true;

CrossDown[i] = High[i] + Range*1.2;

if(i<=2 && Alerts && !downalert)

{

Alert (Symbol()," ",Period()," Mins  Sidus SHORT ");

if ( Email_Alerts ) { SendMail("Sidus SHORT "+Symbol(),""); }

downalert=true;

upalert=false;

}

}

}

return(0);

}

It says in the system that you should close your position and go in the opposite direction once the red tunnel boundarys cross, but what if the WMAs are moving in the same direction as the trend you were in before?

For example, say I have had a long position open for a while. At one point, the tunnels cross or come close enough to form one line. If both the WMAs have fallen a little under the tunnel, and are heading up as the tunnel crosses/comes close, does that mean I should keep going with the long trend or close and open a short position?

Hopefully that question makes sense. I'll reword it if I need to.

--- 帖子 #1689 ---
Cougarelite,

I have been experimenting with the Sidus method since Sidus posted it.

First you should close your position when the 5 WMA crosses under the 12 WMA.  If you wait to close when the 18 and 28 EMAs become close or cross, then you lose pips in the process.

Remember that the red tunnel (18 and 28 EMAs) show the longer term trend.  The blue WMAs indicate the daily momentary fluctuations in trading.

I tend to close when the WMAs cross in the opposite direction, but reopen if they cross back in the same direction of the red tunnel.  I watch for narrowing of the red tunnel to indicated that trend is changing and therefore the likelyhood of changing from long to short or viceversa.

Hopefully that helps.

Yo Pip Dog-

With the tools available here on the forum, you can set up MT with a Sidus crossover alert that will make the noise of your choice <grin>. Someone even posted a .wav file that sounds like the ones they use in old movies when a battle ship is sounding Battle Stations! That'll pull you away from any TV program or put you on the floor if you are asleep.LOL

As mentioned MT is free and wow it is great. Take it from someone whose bought a few commercial charting programs for futures and equity trading. The best thing about MT is the indicators that have been written for about any purpose. You can download a insert them to tailor a trading system the way that suits you. The learning curve is not bad and worth all the time you put into it. I've NEVER had a crash and I keep up two charts on all major pairs, my broker's window, a chat window and another charting program for trading the Dow Emini. I use a moderately powered laptop from Gateway that I paid $600 for a couple months ago. I do have DSL but it's the "lite" version, not max broadband.

--- 帖子 #1707 ---
Seems that this system has kept a core belief but there are a lot of variations on that theme. If you read the entire thread you'll see how it has morphed about. It seems pretty much agreed that the moving avgs. are the 12 and 5 now and that they are standard EMAs. The crossover of the two are the primary signal. Added to this is the RSI. Some have kept the 21 as I believed was orginal but others (Sidus himself?) have changed to the 14 RSI. Actually there is very little difference when you set them up side by side. The rule on the RSI is it should be >than the 50 line to go long and <than the 50 to be short. (Or at least headed that way) Others have tweaked it with various occilators that all are meant to show over/under sold conditions.Some may be using other favorite indicators based on anything from candle bar sizes to moon phases. Whatever!

When trading any system keep your wits about you. Don't blindly take every signal. Sometimes you can get wipsawed mercilessly during a consolidation. Also you can crossover into a support or resistance zone that will bounce you back on your tushy and then some. The Sidus (also the Bagovino) are change or return to trend following systems. They work best with a strong dose of common sense. I'd not personally run either on and auto trading EA. Just my opinion. I tend to be a control freak and like to push my own buttons on trades and the TV remote <grin>. This method looks good on daily time frame and hourly. I've not monitored or traded it on any others. I have looked at it on shorter TF but because of the pip spreads involved you will get dimed out or take too little profit many times to make it worthwhile. I don't know any scalping method that I'd use on the Forex. I do scalp the Dow Emini (YM) with success but with an entirely different system from Ryan Watts (google).

--- 帖子 #1716 ---
If you go to the first post you can download the instructions.  All you need to do is put in 4 MAs onto a chart and set them as a template.  It is an 18 and 28 EMA, both red, and your 5 WMA which is blue and your 8 WMA which is yellow.  Admittedly some of us are using a 12 WMA rather than an 8 WMA, but you can read the whole thread and make up your mind or just pick one and try it out.  Sidus uses these on a 1H chart, although he says that a 30M chart is acceptable, but that there will be more whipsaws.

For the complete information on the use of the indicator, once you have it loaded into your computer, you will just have to read the download from that first post.

Good luck and good trading.

--- 帖子 #1780 ---
Eagle

WMA significa "Weighted Moving Average"

Un metodo impiegato per i dati regolari nelle serie cronologiche in cui ogni osservazione che è avuta una media è data un peso che riflette la relativa importanza relativa nella calcolazione della media.

--- 帖子 #1801 ---
Just finished reading the whole thread, two very useful tips i found regarding the system were:

For entry: Wait for the candle after the cross-candle to close with the same color and above (BUY) or below (SELL) i.e. waiting for the trend to establish itself in order to avoid whipsaws.

For exit: Take profits when 5 & 8 WMA cross and not the 18 & 28 EMA.

BTW the system looks very smooth on 4h TF. Less trades, monitoring & stress :-)

--- 帖子 #1815 ---
Hi Group,

after a couple of weeks of experimenting and trading with this system, I'd like to share how I adapted this method to 'make it my own':

- I've added a 21-period Bollinger Band to the price chart.

- I put a 21-period Bollinger Band on top of the RVI, i.e. the Bollinger Bands now show to what extend the RVI has extreme values within its last 21-period value range.

- I've added a Williams-%R over 89 periods, using -10 and -90 threshold settings.

What does this allow me to do?

Using both the RVI and price action positions relative to their Bollinger Bands,  I can now trade down to the 15-min interval.  If both are outside of their Bands and RVI turns back into the bands, opening a position in that direction is warranted.

As on these short time frames 'the tunnel' with their default settings don't work all that well I use Williams-%R to still keep an eye on the potential big moves.

Please let me know what you think...

cheers

Ohka

--- 帖子 #1837 ---
First I am a fan of Vegas method even if it is criticised on other forums. I discovered the sidus method which is a derivative system of Vegas Tunnel method about 5 months ago. The main problem with tunnel method is when you are in choppy market (no trend). And to avoid these periods of ranging market, you should use a good filter. You can see at Vegas method for a help. With Sidus method, I wait for the 5WMA crosses 8WMA and then price closes above the tunnel. I then enter the market and put my stop loss according to the last swing low / last support / PPZ / or no more than 50 pips. It depends on your style of trading and the money you are ready to lose (money management). For the exit, I use Fib levels and divergence on oscillator (RSI or Stoch) with PA. I can tell you I am profitable now thanks to the tunnel method. I have a friend who use the 24EMA applied on highs and lows as a tunnel (1h TF)....he is very very profitable!!!

--- 帖子 #1842 ---
little about candlestick

Candlestick.

High Body = Reflecting MAJOR trendline

High Tail = Reflects the indicator changes direction / Trendline.

Psikology Market at Candlestick

Tail Up = Reflects interest Sellers / Bears gained

Tail Down = Reflects interest Buyers / Bulls strengthened

Price Open / Closed = Reflects resistance Resistance / Support

Body = Reflects Volume and Trendline

Momentum = Momentum during Break Resistance

--- 帖子 #1850 ---
Aaaarrgh - I did it again. Judging a strategy on behalf of nice looking moving averages. I do know that price MUST be analyzed firstly. Why don't I do that right away? Stupid me.

So what is wrong with this picture from the manual and with this strategy? If the circles is entry and exit points - then watch the entry and exit price of the corresponding bar at those specific points. You will see, that all trades a loosers!!! He advice stoploss at 10 - 15 pips. That means in practise, that he will never reach the closing points on the circles. Then why mention them at all? You will never be able to trade this strategy as a Close in one direction and at the same time open in the opposite direction. At least not watching this picture from the manual . Using the 5 / 8 crosses will totally spoil the red crosses. Strategy is not clear at this matter. So the only way to trade this will be to enter at the crosses of 5 / 8 OR 18 / 28. You have to choose - you cannot do both! And exits must be a trailing stop. I think 15 pips is ok.

So the strategy is reduced to a moving average cross strategy - nothing else. Sorry!

Lesson learned guys: Moving averages or other indicators can often seduce your eyes. But they will be loosers in practice.

So, don't I use Moving averages myself. Oh yes, but not standing alone. MA is vital in some of my profitable robots.
